This guide does n o t describe t h e\nd e t a i l s of the ATLAS c a p a b i l i t i e s , b u t provides an i n t r o d u c t i o n\nt o the new u s e r of ATLAS to t h e level a t which the complete a r r a y\nof c a p a b i l i t i e s described i n t h e ATLAS U s e r % Manual can be\nexploited f u l l y\n\n.\n\nThe ATLAS System is o p e r a t i o n a l on t h e Control Data\nCorporation (CDC) 6600/CYBER computers i n t h e batch, on-line,\ni n t e r a c t i v e , and mixed computing environments\nIt i s a modular\nsystem of computer codes w i t h common e x e c u t i v e and data-base\nmanagement components,\nf\n\nAn i n t e g r a t e d sof tware-system architecture is used t o provide\ncost e f f e c t i v e analyses of s t r u c t u r e s i n a small or l a r g e problem\nenvironment, The system provides an e x t e n s i v e s e t of generalpurpose t e c h n i c a l programs With a n a l y t i c a l c a p a b i l i t i e s including\ns t i f f n e s s , stress, loads, mass, s u b s t r u c t u r i n g , s t r e n g t h design,\nunsteady aerodynamics, v i b r a t i o n , and f l u t t e r analyses\nThe\ns t i f f n e s s finite-element s t r u c t u r a l - a n a l y s i s approach is used\nwherein t h e p h y s i c a l p r o p e r t i e s of the s t r u c t u r e a r e r e p r e s e n t e d\nby a finite number of i d e a l i z e d elements,\nThe sequence and mode of execution of s e l e c t e d program\nm o d u l e s are c o n t r o l l e d by a common user-oriented language,\nI n t e r a c t i v e u s e r i n t e r f a c e s are provided f o r performing\nexecution-control\ndata-f i l e e d i t i n g , and graphical-display of\nselected data. Communication of d a t a between program nlodules is\nperformed automatically by the ATLAS data-base manager, which can\nalso be used t o manipulate d a t a for i n t e r f a c i n g selected modules\nw i t h e x t e r n a l programs.\nfi\n\nModel-definition i n p u t data are w r i t t e n i n a problem-oriented\nlanguage.\nInput-data generation o p t i o n s and input-data checks\nprovided by t h e preprocessors minimize t h e amaunt of d a t a and\nflowtime f o r problem d e f ~ i t i a n / v e r i f i c a t i o n , Postprocessors\nallow selected d a t a t o be extracted, manipulated, and displayed\nv i a on-line o r o f f - l i n e p r i n t s and p l o t s fox monitoring and\nv e r i f y i n g problem s o l u t i o n s .\n\nThe design 02 the ATLAS System has been based primarily on\nt h e needs of t h e analyst i n performing s i n g l e or multidisciplined\nanalysis/design tasks. From the t e c h n i c a l and system reviews\nwith the users, extended versions of t h e system have been\nreleased for general use. In t h e a n t i c i p a t i o n of extending t h e\nsystem c a p a b i l i t i e s , a h i g h degree of f l e x i b i l i t y and g e n e r a l i t y\nhas been incorporated i n t o many segments of the system,\n\nI\n\niii\n\nCONTENTS\nPage\n\n.. .. . . . ..\nATLAS SYSTEM\n. . .. .. - .\n- S S E DESIGN\nYTM\n2\nUSERbS\nAND\n2.3 RANDOM ACCESS FILE\n. -.\n2 - 4 SYSTEM DEMONSTRATION PROBLEMS\n2.5 LOADS\n2-6\n. .- . .\n\n1.0 INTRODUCTION\n\n2.0\n\nI\n\n. .. . .\n0\n\nt.?\n\n.\n)\n\nI.\n\nm\n\nMODULE THEORY\nDESIGN MODULE THEORY\nSNARR USER6S MANUAL.\n\ne\n\n.\nr\n\nt\n\nc\n\n. ., . . Total Weight vs. Design Cycle Number\n\n8.112\n\n9-0 SNARK LANGUAGE\n\nTo simplify the s o l u t i o n of matrix related problems n o t\nd i r e c t l y solvable by the i n t e g r a t e d c a p a b i l i t i e s of the ATLAS\nSystem, t h e high l e v e l matrix-oriented language, SNARK, is\nprovided by ATLAS.. The SNARK package includes t h e SNaRK\nlanguage, the SNARK precompiler, and t h e SNARK l i b r a r y support\nroutines. It i s used extensively throughout t h e ATLAS System and\ncan be used within ATLAS c o n t r o l decks t o perform many matrix\noperations including a l g e b r a i c rnatrix manipulation, matrix i n p u t\nand output on e i t h e r random o r s e q u e n t i a l f i l e s , management of\nmatrix s t o r a g e i n core, and management of the ATLAS data base,\nTable 9-1 shows a summary of the SNARR commands, Detailed\ndescriptions of SNARX dre presented i n the SHARK U s e r h s Manual\nATLAS documentation\nI\n\n4\n\n9.1\n\nCONTROL PROGRAM APPLICATIONS\n\nThe ATLAS Control Program, as created from the user-written\nexecution-control data deck, provides c a p a b i l i t i e s f o r performing\nt h e following functions :\n\na)\n\nDefine t h e sequence and mode of execution of selected\nATLAS modules\n\nb)\n\nControl ATLAS data-management functions\n\ne)\n\nPerform s p e c i a l a n a l y s e s not d i r e c t l y supported by t h e\nATLAS System\n\nd)\n\nPerform data i n t e r f a c e s between t h e ATLAS System and\nexternal programs\n\nThe first t w o functions are supported by t h e ATLAS System\nexecution-control language whereas, i n general, t h e l a s t two\nfunctions require the use of SNARK and FORTRAM, The primary\n\nfunction of SNARR i n performing s p e c i a l a n a l y s i s and interface\nc a p a b i l i t i e s is in t h e area of data management and matrix\nalgebra- These functions are discussed i n t h e following\nsections.\n9.1\n\n-\n\n1\n\nData Manasement\n\nWhenever u s e r defined c a p a b i l i t i e s are defined i n an ATLAS\ncontrol deck, t h e need t o manipulate data within the ATLAS data\nbase is present. T h i s may involve simply reading a data matrix,\nadding data to the data base, or modifying the e x i s t i n g data and\nreplacing it i n t h e data base, The reading and replacement of\ndata matrices, and t h e in-core management of the accessed data\n\naxe handled by SMARX- The SNARK command RDMATRB, f o r example, is\nused t o access a s p e c i f i c d a t a m a t r i x within the ATLAS data base,\nThe matrix i s read i n t o core and s t o r e d i n blank common w i t h any\nother data matrices read o r defined by t h e Control Program. All\nd a t a matrices are s t o r e d i n blank common between the l a s t address\nloaded and t h e s t a r t of the random access tables, This s t o r a g e\narea is managed by SNWiK i n such a way a s t o prevent w a s t e d space\nand to eliminate the need f o r the user to know where, in blank\ncommon, a given matrix i s located, The user-assigned position\nnumber of a d a t a matrix does not n e c e s s a r i l y correspond t o i t s\nposition i n core. When matrices change s i z e , o r a r e w r i t t e n out,\ncreated, or deleted, SNARK may reshuffle the position of matrices\ni n core. Abrtracr\n\nThis document describes some of the many analytical capabilities provided by\nthe ATLAS integrated structural analysis and design system. The example\ndata and fundamental technical considerations presented in this guide are\nintended to help orieni the engineer in using ATLAS, and to direct him in\nusing the other ATLAS System documentation. ATLAS is operational on the\nControl Data Corporation (CDC) 6600/CYBER computers in the batch, on-line,\nand interactive modes. It is a modular system of computer codes with common\nexecutive and data-base management components. The system provides an extensive set of generai-purpose technical programs with analytical capabilities\nlncluding stiffness, stress, loads, mass, substructuring, strength desfgn,\nunsteady aerodynamics, vibration, and flutter analyses. , The sequence and\nmode of execution of selected program modules are controlled by a common\nuser-oriented language. Execution of selected modules with external interfaced programs is supported by the ATLAS data-base\'and ATLAS data manager.\nInteractive user interfaces are provided for performing execution-control,\ndata-file editing, and graphical-display of selected data. Model-definition\ninput data are written in a problem-oriented language. Input-data generation\noptions and input-data checks provided by the preprocessors minimizk t ;\nh\namount of data and flowtime for problem &efinition/verification. Postr off-line prints and plots for monitoring and verifying problem\n\nUnclassified\n\n\'for\n\n-\n\nUnlimited\n\nby %heN J ~ J W ~\n\'IeChnrUI Information k r v r e . Simngfteld.
